New Year's Essays Two

Northeast Problem and the World Powers: Light 18

Before the World War, the issues were in Europe, in the Atlantic Ocean; international disputes were in Europe, while the colonial market scramble in Asia and Africa was at the forefront of these issues, the object of contention, but the core was still in Europe, and the competition was mainly between major powers such as England, Germany, France, Russia, Austria-Hungary. The struggle for maritime rights was in the Atlantic Ocean, and the Western Hemisphere (North and South America) was Europe's treasure trove. By the time of the Great War, Europe's development had naturally reached its peak, that is, the development of the eastern shore of the Atlantic had reached its zenith. During the European War, the United States rose sharply, leveraging all its inherent abilities, and suddenly seized the reins of global finance.

However, since the Great War, the international situation has undergone tremendous changes, with the Pacific Ocean becoming the great stage for global competition: the antagonism between Japan and the United States, the disharmony between Britain and the United States, France's desire to open up territories in the Far East, coupled with the rise of Chinese nationalism, and the development of the Soviet Union, not a single event is without mutual conflict. Especially after the Mukden Incident, it has aroused serious attention from all countries in the world, coinciding with a period of deepening economic panic; Japan wants to use external expansion to overcome its domestic difficulties, arousing the primitive aggressive psychology of its people; at the same time, it also knows that in late 1931 and early 1932, Britain and the United States were focusing all their energy on economic recovery, so no matter what violent means are used to deal with China, the powers would not use real strength to intervene. It has a considerable understanding of China's strength, and it knows that China is also struggling in extreme difficulties and will never be able to muster all its strength to deal with it. Therefore, it occupies Liaoning and Jilin to test the waters, and then further attacks Jinzhou. Britain has always been very cautious, especially thorough in its consideration of Far Eastern issues, initially believing that Japan would never dare to swallow the Northeast, as long as its economic interests were not harmed, then it would naturally stand idly by. The United States did not initially believe that the September 18th Incident would continue to escalate, until the Japanese army invaded Jinzhou before issuing a warning to Japan on December 24, 1931, but it still could not prevent the expansion of the incident in the slightest. The January 28th Shanghai Incident occurred and even affected the international market. The United States, without a special base in the Chinese market, naturally felt threatened; even Britain was worried about the erosion of the market along the Yangtze River: so on January 30, Britain and the United States jointly protested to Japan, but focused on the safety of British and American lives and property, and the normal state of the concessions, without mentioning how to eliminate the war of aggression or stop the war. At that time, the United States was the most vehemently angry, but it only stopped at anger. After the Shanghai war, even the degree of anger decreased, the reasons being: first, the deepening of the economic panic in the United States, second, the European countries not only were not in harmony with the United States but even had quite conflicting implications, and third, the existing military strength of the United States could not go to war with Japan, and the United States did not have the necessity or determination to go to war with Japan; so although it was very angry, it could no longer have further expressions. The Soviet Union and Northern Manchuria originally had a relationship of interdependence. If Japanese imperialism succeeded in Northern Manchuria, the area along the Chinese Eastern Railway would certainly not be controlled by the Soviet Union, and Siberia would also feel serious pressure; but on the one hand, it had to be wary of the united opposition of the capitalist countries, and moreover, it was striving to complete the Five-Year Plan, so as long as the Japanese army did not cross the Soviet border and invade Siberia! Then the Soviet Union would always adopt an extremely calm and bystander attitude, watching how rampant Japan was, watching how the conflict changed, watching how Britain and Japan joined hands, and then deciding its foreign policy. In fact, the Soviet Union's prudence, thoroughness, alertness, and tenacity in diplomatic strategy are not behind any country in the current world.

During the period when the sound of cannons shook the sky in Shanghai, the Disarmament Conference opened in Geneva on February 2nd, with a total of fifty-five countries participating, and more than a thousand participants, truly an unprecedented grand event. The purpose was, needless to say, to reduce armaments, but based on the situation on the day the conference opened, simply judging by the facts of the aggression in Shanghai and the continued bloodshed in the Northeast, it was enough to expose the huge contradictions of this conference. Fundamentally, it was already a story of putting on a facade. First, France's security guarantees and Germany's demand for equal armaments were opposed to each other; second, there was the struggle for hegemony between Japan and the United States in the Pacific, especially Japan was expanding its submarines, and the United States insisted on [Open Door, Equal Opportunity], which in reality required a strong naval force as a backing, and Britain was also not at ease with this situation, and the construction of the port of Singapore had not slackened; third, the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, it was rumored that it paid special attention to heavy industry to develop military industries, how could European countries and even Japan be at ease with this. Moreover, the major countries were all striving to replenish their armaments: airplanes, tanks, long-range artillery, pocket warships, etc., were all very sharp weapons. In addition, Japan in the East exhausted its efforts in military affairs, everywhere demonstrating its iron fist of military adventure, although not directly challenging, at least using an iron hand to crush peace, and using machine guns to block the road to peace. Therefore, although the Disarmament Conference had great momentum, it was ultimately hindered by the above-mentioned mountain of contradictions, and even treaties like the Washington Treaty and the London Naval Agreement could not be established.

Although it is not easy for the European and American powers to find compromise solutions in military affairs, it is also not easy to achieve temporary relaxation and reduce the burden of military spending; if they can find new reconciliation schemes in the economy, it may not be a better method than this. Originally, they were prepared at the League of Nations Administrative Council on December 10th to seek an economic outlet in the East. The League of Nations Investigation Team came to the East, saying it was for the Sino-Japanese conflict, and to investigate the truth of the Manchurian Incident with a fair attitude. However, when the League of Nations Investigation Team came to the East, it spent twelve days in Japan, and when it first landed in China in Shanghai, it spent another twenty-five days in Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Yichang, Wanhsien, and other places, then ten days in Beiping, and only on April 20th did it go to the Northeast to spend forty-four days investigating. After June 5th was the time for editing the report. The contents of the Investigation Team's report (there were criticisms everywhere in the world, and this newspaper also made fair criticisms, which will not be repeated). We only need to know that the team first circled in the Yangtze River basin and Beiping to know its true meaning. Therefore, the conclusion of the Investigation Team's report was to place [Manchuria] under the guidance of the International Advisory Conference. It is obvious that it is to achieve international coordination, especially the world's major powers (the United States' secret help is especially powerful) to have Japan implement the [Open Door] and [Equal Opportunity] declarations, and to let Japan cede some of the rights it has seized in [Manchuria] to various countries, so that the surplus goods can find a new market and there is hope for a turnaround in the economic panic. However, the [Open Door] advocated by Japan was originally a means to ease the active intervention of the powers; when the diplomatic situation eased, it would take back the words of [Open Door] and advocate [East Asian Monroe Doctrine]. Therefore, the investigation of the Investigation Team only stopped at investigation, and no other significance or role could be found.

Therefore, the opposition between Japan and the United States became more and more clear, the relationship between Britain and the United States was not satisfactory, and Europe was also brewing a crisis. Especially the cancer that the world has recognized for ten years, the German reparations, since the US President initiated the postponement of reparations payments in June 1931, in the past year, the world economy has not only not improved, but even has little hope of improving: Germany has become even more severe, and in terms of unemployed workers, it has increased from 4 million in June of the previous year to 5.5 million in June of this year. Therefore, the reparations conference was held in Lausanne on June 16th. After several discussions, although the reparations were not completely waived, the world's cancer has been cut open; in name, the reparations were renamed the European Reconstruction Fund, the amount was reduced by 29/30ths, and it would still need to be compensated after the market recovered three years later. Item 5 of the Lausanne Conference Resolution also included a clause calling for a world economic conference to be convened by the League of Nations, and solutions to currency issues, tariff issues, and war debts should be found in the world economic conference. Although it was attached with a proviso that if war debts were not reduced, the Lausanne Treaty would have to be reconsidered; but this was clearly a means to deal with the United States, and would not have much impact on the Lausanne Treaty in reality. During the Lausanne Conference era, even though there were various discordant situations, the European countries were generally united, Britain and France naturally followed suit, and Germany also understood the relationship of international politics and made relative concessions; looking at the scene at that moment, capitalism truly had a symbol of revival. From the establishment of the Lausanne Treaty (June 29th) to the British Imperial Economic Conference (July 21st), the time was only one month, and the spirit of coordination was almost completely dispersed. Indeed, what was discussed in Ottawa was within the British Empire: the political and economic issues between Britain and its self-governing dominions and colonies: but Britain abandoned its traditional economic policy 丨丨 Free Trade and adopted protectionist trade, and there was an even more special phenomenon, which was the economic alliance of the British Empire. The impact of this alliance, not to mention in Britain itself, gave great stimulus to countries around the world: Japan in the East wanted to annex the three northeastern provinces to form a [Japan-Manchuria Economic Alliance]: the United States would certainly further strengthen the American [Monroe Doctrine]; France, although unable to revive the European economic alliance for a time, was even more obsessed with self-sufficiency and closed-doorism; the Soviet Union was originally a separate system, and the fifteen years of struggle

Page 9

Page 10

Page 11

Page 12

the more it intensifies its efforts to build a socialist country on its own. Moreover, the national capital of the colonies has gradually risen, the revolutionary movements in South American countries, the awakening of India, and the subtle growth of Chinese nationalism are all dramatic phenomena of the complex opposition between countries in the current world.

Therefore, the so-called union of capitalist countries against Russia has ultimately become propaganda more than anything else. Of course, we admit that the capitalist countries do have malice towards the Soviet Union, and they really do not want the existence of the Soviet Union, but they are still paying attention to the development of this promising market in the Soviet Union, so except for the United States, several major countries have normal diplomatic relations and business dealings with it, even if the United States does not have commercial relations, then the so-called anti-Russianism is actually much milder compared to the mutual opposition of capitalist countries (such as the opposition between Germany and France, the opposition between France and Italy, and the opposition between the United States and Japan). The Japanese-Soviet fisheries agreement in mid-August, followed by the Japanese-Soviet oil agreement, and then the Japanese-Soviet understanding during Matsuoka Yosuke's activity in Moscow. Especially important are the [Non-Aggression Treaty] between France and the Soviet Union, followed by the non-aggression treaty between Poland and the Soviet Union; on the one hand, this does not seem to have any major meaning, but on the other hand, it breaks the fifteen-year gap between France and the Soviet Union. France will shift from preventing Russia to developing closer commercial relations with the Soviet Union, and so will Poland; as for the Soviet Union! Then the western front will be calm from now on. All in all, the capitalist countries' vigilance against the Soviet Union cannot be without (even if there is, it is similar to the mutual vigilance of capitalist countries, and is not worth mentioning), and the anti-Russian movement has at least been eased.

But on the other hand, Britain and France were originally consistent, but they went their separate ways in order to repay the war debts due, and a huge storm broke out between France and the United States over the war debts. Even the US Senate and House of Representatives proposed retaliatory measures against France. This economic dispute caused a rift in Franco-American relations, which had a negative impact on the recovery of the market. Since Britain and France took different steps, and Franco-American relations deteriorated, and disputes occurred between Italy and Yugoslavia, in other words, the opposition between France and Italy worsened. These situations, even if they do not lead to serious consequences, will at least affect the world economy and make it more difficult to recover. And the increase in unemployed workers, the shrinking of the market, the economic alliance of closed-doorism 丨丨 the prevalence of self-sufficiency, is the first characteristic of the international situation in 1932, and the struggle to compete for the market, to advocate equal benefit sharing, and to monopolize is the second. (December 31, 1932)

The Northeast Incident over the Past Year: Du Liang 19

Time flies like an arrow. The past scene will never return. The humiliating and disgraceful Republic of China's 21st year has ended its ominous years. The sunshine that is dawning in the 22nd year is just brewing its future vitality. At this time of the New Year, we also want to express our inner expectations. What kind of thoughts and feelings can be used as a warning? Tracing back to the launch of the September 18th Incident, the soil of the three provinces was completely destroyed in an instant. The vastness of the lost territory and the speed of the loss are truly unheard of in this era, and rarely seen in history. All those who belong to the human race must have the thought of wiping out the shame and seeking survival. At the end of the 20th year, how could we not expect the strength of the 21st year to restore the lost territory and restore the rivers and mountains to their former glory. After hesitating for a year, what did the facts reward us? The vast land of the Northeast has been nibbled away, and the essence of Shanghai has been destroyed again. The government authorities only have the call for resistance, and the League of Nations only engages in empty talk on paper, watching the Japanese warlords act arbitrarily and recklessly, waving their hands freely, and have not been able to restrain them in the slightest. At this point, the people of the country should be disgusted with the unreliability of other forces, and urgently seek to save themselves. However, at the mention of self-salvation, there are some negative phenomena that disappoint and discourage us. The brave soldiers outside the Pass are fighting bloody battles against the powerful enemy, while the soldiers inside the Pass are fighting to seize territory. After the catastrophe, the disaster-stricken are shivering in the cold and desolate wind, while the playboy princes are frolicking in the arena of singing and dancing. Comparing the two scenes, the insightful people are truly overwhelmed with the fear of perishing together. However, today, can we still use the way of mutual blame and accusations to shirk our responsibilities? Hundreds of millions of people should unite and work together to fulfill their promises. Starting from the New Year's Day of the 22nd year, we must cleanse our hearts and minds, and temper ourselves. Starting from the New Year's Day of the 22nd year, we must unite as one to resist foreign aggression. To only curse the past is not enough to cover up the past sins. To have empty hopes for the future may not necessarily lead to a way out. Learning from the past failures and encouraging the future, it is not too late to mend the fold after losing the sheep. I will take advantage of the spare time of this newspaper's New Year's Day special edition to summarize the main points of the Northeast situation over the past year, as a call to action and to show that we have not forgotten.

After the September 18th Incident, Liaoning established a temporary provincial government in Jinzhou. The Japanese side saw this as an obstacle and wanted to get rid of it. Ever since the Inukai Cabinet was formed and Araki Sadao succeeded as the Minister of the Army, their aggression against us has become more active. The British, American, and French envoys to Japan successively sent政牒 to the Japanese government, advising it to avoid the conflict in Jinzhou. The Japanese government replied that it had no intention of attacking Jinzhou, but secretly made every effort to arrange military operations against Jinzhou. In late December of the 20th year, a large number of Japanese planes bombed the vicinity of Jinzhou and successively captured Panshan Goubangzi. By January 2nd of the 21st year, Jinzhou was lost. The Japanese army then advanced and occupied Lianshan Suizhong, using the Jinzhou-Chaoyang line to invade Rehe, but was blocked by the volunteer army and failed. In order to divert the attention of the Chinese people, the Japanese increased troops in the Eastern Provinces on the one hand, and actively provoked in Shanghai on the other, which led to the January 28th Incident. (For details of the Shanghai War, see another article, which will not be repeated here.) By early February, Harbin was also captured. At this point, the Japanese wanted to implement a puppet policy, using traitors such as Zang Shiyi, Xi Qia, and Zhang Jinghui to support Puyi in organizing the so-called Manchurian State and establishing a false capital in Changchun. Puyi assumed the false post of ruler on March 9th and issued a declaration. The Japanese also incited them to forcibly take over the customs and intercept the salt tax. Ma Zhanshan was known for his anti-Japanese achievements. At the beginning of the organization's establishment, he once feigned compliance and accepted a false post. In early April, he secretly went to Heihe, telegraphed to resist Japan, and announced the evidence that the false country was established by Japanese conspiracy. At that time, volunteer armies rose up everywhere. Leaders such as Ding Chao, Li Du, Feng Zhanhai, and Wang Delin all contacted Ma and others, calling themselves the National Salvation Army or the Self-Defense Army, and acted separately to resist Japan. Suddenly, Shenyang was in danger, and suddenly, Harbin was besieged. Famous cities and towns were repeatedly recovered. The volunteer army was powerful and the Japanese were exhausted. In late July, the false country forcibly took over the Northeast post offices. At the same time, the Japanese army once again advanced towards Rehe, using the Ishimoto case as an excuse to send planes to bomb the villages and towns on the Rehe border. The great powers were also very wary of the Japanese's arrogance. US Secretary of State Stimson repeatedly stated that he would not recognize the status of the Northeast created by force. Japan ignored this and went its own way, and its antipathy towards the United States became even greater. In early August, the Japanese appointed Muto Nobuyoshi as the commander of the Kwantung Army, and Honjo Shigeru was transferred back to Japan. At the same time, Muto was also appointed as the special envoy to Manchuria and notified the League of Nations to prepare for the recognition of the false country. As for September 15th, it disregarded everything and formally recognized the false Manchurian State. The two sides signed the Japan-Manchuria Protocol. The false country also announced the independence of the customs. Until September, Su Bingwen's road protection team stationed in the Chinese Eastern Railway revolted and occupied Manchuria Station, which boosted the anti-Japanese situation. Su and Ma communicated with each other and advanced on Qiqihar. The Japanese army suffered repeated setbacks. The Japanese military headquarters instructed the troops stationed in Shenyang to use both bribery and force against the volunteer army. At the same time, it continued to arm and immigrate to the three eastern provinces to increase its strength. On the one hand, it repeatedly induced Su Bingwen to negotiate peace. Su sternly refused and persisted for many days. In the end, due to the lack of ammunition and food, he was forced to retreat into Russian territory. At this point, the Japanese army claimed that there was no need to worry about Northern Manchuria and wanted to advance into Rehe with all its heart. At the time of writing, the situation on the border was extremely tense. It is difficult to predict what will happen in the future. They harbor the ambition of a giant pig and a long snake and have the ambition of swallowing and eating. If they are not stopped in the阴, there will be no end. How can the people of the country still not rise up and pursue the final resistance? Under the overturned nest, there are no intact eggs.

Page 13

Current Affairs Commentary

New Year's Greetings from Guangzhou 20

With great difficulty, and yet, very luckily, the year 1932 slipped past the edge of terror and destruction last night. This morning, every politician, financier, and entrepreneur in capitalist countries seems to be able to congratulate each other with tearful smiles, [Oh, thank God, we have struggled through another year.]

However, the past year of 1932 did not rid the world of the misfortune of panic. The newly arrived 1933 is not necessarily a [symbol of the world's turning point]. History has already arranged a [destination] for this world. At present, the world is like struggling laboriously in a bottomless dark cave. Only by struggling to the end of the darkness can one hope to see the dawn. That is to say, although 1932 luckily slipped away last night, we have not yet reached a year in which we can [turn tears into smiles].

Let us try to take the facts left in front of us by the past year of 1932 and make a rough review: First, from an economic point of view, 1932 was the fourth year after the outbreak of the world economic panic. Of course, no matter from which aspect we observe it, it was only the deepening of the panic and the intensified development of the crisis. Just in terms of the unemployed masses around the world, according to statistics published by the U.S. Department of Commerce, among the 311 million people in Europe, the number of unemployed was 11,378,000, and among the 123 million people in the United States, the number of unemployed was 11,400,000. According to the annual report of Thomas, Director of the International Labor Office, in the world unemployment crisis, one out of every 28 people is deprived of their means of survival. From this huge number of unemployed, we can clearly see the depth of the world economic panic.

Moreover, these figures are still the result of the [manufacturing] of clever politicians. They are discounted remnants, not the real numbers. We only see that whether it is the United States, the richest place in the world, or the United Kingdom, a capitalist developed country, or Switzerland, known for its peace, there is a miserable cry of hunger and cold everywhere, and there is a roar of [demanding work, demanding bread] everywhere. London has been threatened twice by 2,500 hungry pedestrians, Washington has been surrounded by veterans of the European War and hunger marchers, and even the [City of Peace, Geneva], where the world's politicians and diplomats gather to discuss [peace], has experienced bloodshed. Cries of complaint, roars of anger, and spontaneous [struggles for survival] have become widespread in the capitalist world. What does this brand-new fact illustrate? Doesn't it further show the deep-seated disease of capitalism? Doesn't it say that the economic panic has set off a terrifying black tide of turmoil in the capitalist world?

However, don't be really deceived by the above facts, thinking that the world is really [poor]. Let me tell you, the world is not poor, and it is feeling quite excessive! Despite the fact that tens of millions of people are crying out in hunger and cold on the one hand, on the other hand, some people are pouring a large amount of milk into rivers and burning a large amount of rice and wheat. Capital is sleeping in warehouses, and goods are piled up in warehouses. They and the hungry and cold masses are increasing their numbers in direct proportion. The hungry and cold masses are crying out [no way out], and they are also crying out [no way out]. Who says the world is poor? But looking at it from another perspective, who can say that the world is not poor? In fact, haven't the majority of the population already fallen into the tragic situation of hunger and cold?

The world is playing the magic of [farce] and [contradiction] in this way. However, look, isn't the hand of the performer of the magic trembling? Isn't it shivering?

This is a rough outline of the world economy in 1932.

○　　○　　○　　○　　○

Putting aside the world, let's take another look at our country.

Speaking of our country, we also feel that everything in front of us is like a tangled thread, and we don't know where to start. From the perspective of foreign troubles, it is very obvious that the situation is getting worse day by day, following the September 18th Incident of the previous year. The Northeast Volunteer Army has gradually shown signs of defeat. Ma Zhanshan's troops have retreated to a corner, Su Bingwen's troops have also retreated into Soviet territory, and Feng Zhanhai's troops are also unable to support themselves. The reason for their failure is the same: [exhausted ammunition and food], [lack of follow-up support]. Rehe is now also reporting an emergency, and North China is also full of rumors and panic. What does this fact illustrate? It clearly points out that taking advantage of the tide of economic panic, Japanese imperialists are actively implementing a gunboat policy against our country, and this aggressive action is actually tacitly approved by the powers. Although by the end of last year, due to the urgency of the diplomatic situation, China and the Soviet Union finally officially resumed diplomatic relations, in fact, the implementation of this diplomatic policy had already missed the opportunity, so it has not yet achieved any success.

Secondly, from the perspective of domestic politics, the characteristics of domestic politics in our country in 1932 were, first, the continued outbreak of internal turmoil. First, there was the Guangdong Rebellion, then the Shandong Rebellion, followed by the Sichuan Rebellion, and the Guizhou Rebellion. In the Guangdong Rebellion, the aircraft that did not dare to resist Japan showed their skills, and [Flying Eagle] was such a sacrifice. Also, in the Shandong Rebellion, according to the Inspection Record of Yexian after the Calamity, it said that [broken wells and ruined walls, a piece of rubble, a hundred years of essence, destroyed in one battle], the misery of its poisoning can be imagined. In the Sichuan War, the people suffered even more miserably. In the battles of Jiangjin, Luzhou, Zizhong, and Chengdu, more than 3,000 innocent people died, and commercial losses in the war zone reached more than 70 million, and other direct losses were countless. Taking the week-long street fighting in Chengdu as an example, the prosperous streets were turned into scorched earth, cultural institutions were destroyed, and the number of student deaths exceeded 1,000. Although there are currently no statistics available for the losses of the Guizhou Rebellion, judging from the poisoning of the Guangdong Rebellion, the Shandong Rebellion, and the Sichuan Rebellion, it is not difficult to imagine.

Furthermore, from an economic point of view: the annual trade deficit has long become an ironclad fact, but this year it will be even more. According to statistics from the International Trade Bureau, this year's trade deficit is at least more than 620 million Customs Taels. Furthermore, social economy is even more [unbearable!]. The floods the year before last destroyed the rural areas completely, and last year's bumper harvest not only failed to support the people's deaths, but also accelerated the destruction of the rural areas. Under the combination of various reasons, the rural areas accelerated bankruptcy, and the decline of major agricultural products such as silk and mulberry was beyond words. There is an extremely obvious fact: Jiangsu has always been known as a rich area in our country, but according to a survey, there are a total of 345 pawnshops in 43 counties in the province, with a total capital of more than 13.6 million, but it is still not enough to cope with the poverty of the rural areas, which can be imagined. If Jiangsu Province is like this, what about other provinces?

In conclusion, the political and economic situation in China in 1932 does show a kind of disease. However, we believe that to diagnose and treat a disease, we must first know where the root cause of the disease lies. If you are sick, you know it yourself. This is unnecessary. At this time, it is the critical moment for the life and death of the Chinese nation. The catastrophe of the future world and the end of the Chinese nation can only be overcome by facing forward and breaking through this black wave. Now we put forward a few points as our New Year's greetings for 1933.

First, only a government and people with a plan that can be implemented diligently can jump out of this economically panicky world and move towards a prosperous future. The success of the Soviet Union's first five-year plan and the start of the second five-year plan today are a model.

Second, under a strict plan, the masses can do their best and do their best, and everyone is doing their best and doing their best for the society, so that they can achieve great results. Not being able to integrate with the masses and not being able to use the great power of the masses is exactly the way to self-destruction.

Third, leaders must strive to have the spirit of sacrificing for the people, and use their great personality to develop their bright attitude and bear the heavy responsibility of this politics. The people must also strive for self-reliance in order to obtain freedom, and must never hope for the gifts of others.

Full Text of the Sino-American Arbitration Treaty 21

Exchanged in Washington on December 15

(Nanjing) The Sino-American Arbitration Treaty was exchanged in Washington on December 15. Our Plenipotentiary Representative Yan Heling telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for instructions from the National Government for filing. The treaty has three articles. Our Plenipotentiary Representative Wu Chaoshu and the American Plenipotentiary Representative Shi Tianchen signed the treaty on June 27, 1930 (June 27, 1930). The full text of the original treaty is as follows:

Article 1. If there is a dispute over international matters between the two contracting countries, and this contracting country makes a request to the other contracting country for rights arising from within or outside the treaty, and this dispute cannot be resolved by diplomatic means, or has been submitted to the Permanent International Committee established in accordance with the treaty signed in Washington on September 15, 1914, and still has not been resolved, and this dispute, due to the application of the principles of law or justice, can be decided, and therefore has the nature of being able to be adjudicated, then, in each case, it shall be decided by special agreement whether to submit it to the Hague Permanent Court of Arbitration established in accordance with the Convention of October 18, 1907, or other equivalent judicial organ. This special agreement shall, if necessary, stipulate the organization of the judicial organ, and shall clearly indicate its powers, state the issues in dispute, and decide the terms of submission to arbitration. The special agreement in each case shall be concluded by China in accordance with the Constitution of the Republic of China, and by the President of the United States with the advice and consent of the Senate of the United States. Article 2. The articles of this treaty shall not be invoked in respect of the following disputes: (a) Those within the scope of the internal affairs of each contracting country; (b) Those involving the interests of a third country; (c) Those belonging to or involving the attitude of the United States towards American issues, i.e., the maintenance of the so-called Monroe Doctrine; (d) Those belonging to or involving the performance of obligations by China in accordance with the Covenant of the League of Nations.

Article 3. This treaty is written in Chinese, English, and French, and shall be ratified by the National Government of China in accordance with the Constitution of China, and by the President of the United States with the advice and consent of the Senate of the United States. The Chinese and English texts shall have equal force, but in case of any discrepancy, the French text shall prevail. The instruments of ratification shall be exchanged in Washington as soon as possible. This treaty shall enter into force from the date of exchange of the instruments of ratification. Thereafter, this treaty shall remain in force until one year after either contracting country has notified the other contracting country in writing of its termination. (Central News Agency telegram on the 31st)

German Authorities Deny Shipping Arms to China 49

National News Agency Berlin, 30th--Recently, the French side has been clamoring that when the former Chinese Ambassador to Germany, Jiang Zuobin, was in office, he was ordered by the National Government to purchase a large amount of arms from German factories. This statement has now been declared by the authorities here to be completely contrary to the facts. Since the end of the European War, only small arms, such as pistols, could be transported abroad from the weapons manufactured in Germany. In recent years, German arms have still been shipped to China from time to time. The reason is that these weapons were mostly from before the European War, and were a large number of guns and cannons seized by the great powers from Germany during the European War and after the signing of the peace treaty, or entered neighboring countries indirectly through various channels, and then arms dealers transported them to China for sale, but they were no longer the property of Germany. As for the orders for the purchase of arms by the commercial counselor of the Chinese Embassy in Berlin, they were not handed over to German factories, but were purchased from other parties, such as a certain Swedish arms factory, which sold 120 anti-aircraft guns in the past two years, and had previously sold hundreds of machine guns, which is one example. Furthermore, France has no reason to protest against German merchants selling arms, because several of France's largest arms factories are managed by German merchants in China, and their business has been quite developed for several years. French factories have been very satisfied with using German merchants to promote their sales, and have supplied the Chinese army with 1,400 machine guns in the past year and a half. These facts are extremely clear in Nanjing and other places, so it is futile for France to reverse the facts in an attempt to deceive the world.

Railway Workers Brewing Industrial Action

Two New Year's Days in One Year 53

A Coincidence for Pacific Ocean Travelers

Lincoln President Steamer, 30th (National News Agency) - The captain of the Lincoln President announced today that passengers on the ship will experience two New Year's Days next year, a rare occurrence in life.

As the ship travels from Shanghai to San Francisco, it will cross the International Date Line (i.e., the 180-degree meridian) on New Year's Day. According to custom, after crossing the line, the date is changed to one day later, reverting back to December 31, 1932. Therefore, there will be two New Year's Days, and the ship will hold two celebrations.

Soviet Foreign Trade: A Dispatch from Vladivostok 56

Soviet foreign trade is also exclusively operated by the state, so the import and export of goods are highly planned. Since the spring of 1918, about fifteen years ago, its foreign trade development has been quite impressive. Before 1920, the capitalist countries first intervened with military force to destroy the revolutionary government and then imposed a strict blockade policy, so the Soviet Union was completely isolated from the outside world and had no trade to speak of. In the middle of 1920, after the blockade was lifted, the total volume of Soviet foreign trade was only 20 million rubles. During the period from 1920 to 1922, Soviet imports were limited to food and daily necessities, as this was a period of great famine. After 1923, domestic production gradually got back on track, and raw materials and semi-manufactured goods began to be imported, while the quantity of consumer goods decreased significantly. In the year 1924 to 1925, the total trade volume was 1.282 billion rubles, of which exports accounted for 559 million and imports accounted for 723 million rubles. During the three years from 1926 to 1929, in addition to raw materials, the import of machinery became a major item, and consumer goods were reduced to less than 10 percent. The total trade volume in 1928-29 was 1.714 billion rubles, of which exports accounted for 878 million and imports accounted for 836 million rubles. Since the end of 1929, the world economic panic occurred, and the international market showed a state of depression. The total trade volume of various countries has decreased, even reduced to one-third. In this situation, the Soviet Union alone was able to avoid this difficulty, so the capitalist countries are jealous of it, saying that it uses a "penetration" policy to undermine the world economy. In 1930, the total trade volume of the Soviet Union was 2.095 billion rubles, with imports accounting for 1.0688 billion and exports accounting for 1.0364 billion rubles. The total trade volume in 1931 also decreased slightly, totaling 1.9162 billion rubles, of which 811.12 million was exports and 1.105 billion was imports. In the first nine months of this year

Page 16

the total trade volume was 963.8 million, with exports at 410.9 million and imports at 552.9 million.

From January to August this year, Soviet exports can be divided into three categories: The first category is agricultural products, with exports of more than 1.3 million tons, valued at more than 76.45 million rubles. The second category is raw materials and semi-manufactured products, with exports of 9.97 million tons, valued at more than 218 million rubles. The third category is manufactured goods, with exports of 67,000 tons, valued at more than 64.35 million rubles. Therefore, in terms of percentage, the first category accounts for 21.3% of total exports, the second category accounts for 60.8%, and the third category accounts for 17.9% of total exports.

Soviet imports can be divided into four categories as follows: The first category is necessities of life, totaling 377,000 tons, worth 43.63 million rubles. The second category is raw materials and semi-manufactured products, totaling 825,000 tons, worth more than 131.83 million rubles. The third category is manufactured goods, totaling 378,000 tons, worth 326 million rubles. The fourth category is livestock, totaling 31,000 tons, worth 5.627 million rubles. In terms of percentage, the first category accounts for 8.6% of the total, the second category accounts for 25.9%, the third category accounts for 64.4%, and the fourth category accounts for 1.1%.

By country, Germany ranked first in foreign trade this year, with a total volume of more than 308 million rubles, of which exports from the Soviet Union to Germany amounted to more than 66.32 million rubles, and imports from Germany amounted to more than 233.75 million rubles. The second largest was Britain and its colonies, with a total trade volume of more than 167.52 million rubles, of which exports accounted for more than 87.89 million rubles and imports accounted for 79.63 million rubles. The third largest was Italy, with a trade volume of more than 36.96 million rubles.

The fourth was the United States, with a trade volume of 31.035 million rubles. The fifth was France, with a total volume of 21.315 million rubles. The sixth was Japan, with a trade volume of 8.537 million rubles. These are all approximate figures as of the end of August.

In summary, the above-mentioned development roughly shows the achievements of the Soviet Union's economic construction over the past ten years. Compared with the decline of our old nation, it is indeed incomparable. (December 12)

Recent Japanese Military Industry 57

Recently, Japan, under the hypnosis of militarism, has been completely plunged into war frenzy. The Satsuma and Choshu cliques are preparing for war almost every day. Since the Manchurian Incident, Japan's military industry has become very active. Factories manufacturing military supplies are working day and night without rest. Some sectors of the business community are thus showing some vitality. From this one aspect alone, one can see what ambitions the Japanese warlords harbor.

Japanese military supply manufacturing factories are divided into two parts: one directly under the Army Department and one directly under the Navy Department. In addition, the steel plant belonging to the Ministry of Commerce and Industry also has close ties with military enterprises. Those belonging to the Army Department include the Army Arsenal Tokyo Factory, Atsuta, Chigusa, Ogura, Pyongyang, and Chungmu Ordnance Factories, Army Arsenal Osaka Factory, Jujo, Itabashi, Oji, Iwahana, Uji, and Powder Factories, Okayama, Tokyo, Chiba, Osaka, Hiroshima, and Ogura Ordnance Branches, Army Aviation Headquarters Technical Department, Supply Department Tokorozawa, Kakamigahara Branch Shimoshizu and Akeno, Tokorozawa Army Flying Schools (manufacturing machinery), Osaka and Ujina Army Food Branches, Army Food Headquarters Sapporo Branch, Senju Woolen Mill, Army Clothing Headquarters, Osaka and Hiroshima Army Clothing Branches, Army Transportation Department (shipbuilding) Technical Headquarters (trial production of weapons), Scientific Research Institute (research on military physics and chemistry), Sanitary Materials Factory (pharmaceutical and medical equipment manufacturing), Communications School, Automobile School, 1st Division Ordnance Department, and other military industries, totaling 38 locations. Those belonging to the Navy Department include Yokosuka, Kure, Hiroshima, Sasebo Naval Factories, Hiratsuka Naval Powder Factory, Maizuru Naval Port Department Works Department, Naval Powder Factory Explosives Department, Ominato Naval Port Department Works Department, Tokuyama Naval Fuel Factory, Tokyo Naval Technical Research Institute, Naval Shipbuilding Headquarters Drafting Workshop, Aviation Headquarters Drafting Workshop (ship, weapon, and aircraft drafting), a total of 12 locations. Those belonging to the Ministry of Commerce and Industry include Yawata Iron Works Headquarters and Tobata and Nishi-Yawata Workshops. Most of these state-run factories are combined with private factories. Since the Japanese army suddenly occupied the three northeastern provinces, the military has been abnormally excited and has been purchasing as much of their products and materials as possible from private factories (especially small and medium-sized industrial and commercial enterprises) under the pretext of "saving the current situation" and "rescuing small and medium-sized industrial and commercial enterprises." On the Army Department side, there are 644 private military supply manufacturing factories that have been directly designated to manufacture military supplies, and 778 indirect subcontractors, totaling 1,422. It is expected that the number of directly designated factories will increase to 1,500 in the next year (1933). The sudden expansion of military industry is truly astonishing.

Since Japan is so eager to prepare for war, it is necessary to pay close attention to the position of the three most important industries for military industry, the metal industry, the machinery and equipment industry, and the chemical industry, in its national industry. According to the Japanese Ministry of Commerce and Industry's survey of the number of factories, the number of workers, and the production value of various industries across the country in 1930 (Showa 5), there is the following table:

In the machinery and equipment industry, iron shipbuilding is the highest. In the chemical industry, mineral fertilizer, soap, and cosmetics manufacturing have the highest production value. These chemical industries are also the easiest to transform into military manufacturing, and their position should not be ignored.

Since the Manchurian Incident, due to the increased manufacturing in the military industry, not only has the military industry itself made special progress, but other related industries have also benefited. Workers' wages have generally tended to increase. In the midst of capitalism's imminent decline, the stimulation of militarism has suddenly presented a good scene of reflection. Japanese soldiers are happily thinking that they have succeeded in their plan. The army's military expenditure of 447.8 million yuan and the navy's military expenditure of 372.6 million yuan total more than 820 million yuan, accounting for 36% of the total national treasury expenditure, the largest increase in military expenditure since the Russo-Japanese War. In addition, there is also a reserve fund of 10 million yuan for the Manchurian Incident and the dispatch fee of 20 million Japanese yen for the entire 6th Division of Kumamoto to be transferred to Manchuria for replacement a week ago, which is not included.

Of this huge military expenditure, the Army Department's expenditure for military industry in 1933 will be 100 million yuan, about twice that of this year. The total amount of funds for saving the current situation by the Ministry of Internal Affairs, the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, and the Ministry of Commerce and Industry is also 160 million yuan. The inevitably sudden turn for the better in the military industry, according to the Bank of Japan's survey in September this year, the index of workers employed in major industries across the country was 74.8 in September, the highest amount this year, an increase of 1.9 compared with the lowest index of 72.9 in January, and an increase of 0.5 compared with the same month last year. Most of this increase is attributed to the military industry, such as machinery manufacturing, which increased by 9% compared with the same period last year, equipment manufacturing increased by 7.6%, metal product manufacturing increased by 1.3%, and rubber manufacturing increased by 6.9%. The wage index in other areas has also increased similarly. According to the Bank of Japan's survey, machinery manufacturing increased by 8.1% in September this year compared with the same period last year, shipbuilding increased by 2.6%, vehicle manufacturing increased by 1.3%, and equipment manufacturing increased by 2.1%. Among them, only metal product manufacturing showed a slight downward trend, but the degree of decline was also very slight. In general, the wage index of military industry clearly has a special increase in the entire industry. At a glance, it is known that it is determined to compete militarily and is the second Germany in the East. In this situation, living abroad in a hotel, looking west at the motherland, I cannot help but feel sad. I wonder what the countries of the world will do with those who disrupt peace. (December 26, 1932, in Tokyo)

The Sichuan War Expected to End 60

Liu Wenhui Defeated, Negotiating Peace with Chongqing

Liu Xiang Initiates Post-War Conference in Neijiang

The Entire 24th Army to Retreat to Xikang

Chongqing Telegraph: Previously, the 24th Army launched an all-out counterattack, occupying Rongxian, Weiyuan, and Qianwei, and advanced directly towards Yibin. Liu Wenhui's plan was to have Zhang Zhifang, Xiong Cihou, and Xu Tingxiu's three brigades press towards Luxian; Wang Yuanhu, Chen Zimin, and Li Yushu's three brigades seize Fushun and Ziliujing; Chen Mingqian, Lin Meipo, and Yu Ruhai's three brigades attack Ziyang from Renshou; and Liu Wencai and others provide support from the center. The remaining troops were to be concentrated in the rear areas of Jiarenjing and other places, hoping to recover the lost territory in one fell swoop. However, Liu Xiang anticipated this move and stationed heavy troops in Luxian and Ziliujing, constructing solid fortifications to resist. Seeing his plan fail, Liu Wenhui ordered all routes to attack simultaneously, resulting in a major battle on the 25th. Liu Xiang deployed all of his aircraft for a massive bombing campaign, resulting in over two thousand military and civilian casualties within the battle zones. The 24th Army's various routes, fearing the Chongqing army's aircraft, dared not advance. Liu Xiang then commanded his forces to launch a large-scale counterattack. The two sides engaged in fierce hand-to-hand combat over ten times in Rongxian, Weiyuan, Qianwei, and other places. Ultimately, due to the Chongqing army's intense air power, the 24th Army's various routes were defeated and retreated to their original defense lines in Jingyan, Jiading, and Renshou. On the 26th, the 21st Army's various routes launched a fierce assault, again occupying Rongxian, Weiyuan, and Qianwei, and advanced towards Jiajing. Fierce battles took place in the areas of Liujia Village, Laijia Village, Lijia Village, and Laojun Terrace. The 24th Army resisted with all its might, using mortar fire to protect their positions. The 21st Army's frontline soldiers, with air cover, launched a fierce assault, advancing like a hot knife through butter. As a result, the 21st Army occupied the 24th Army's first line of defense between Jiajing. At the same time, Li Qixiang and Luo Zezhou's forces launched a fierce attack on the Renshou front, engaging Chen Mingqian's brigade of the 24th Army in a fierce battle lasting approximately seven hours. Chen's troops were unable to withstand the attack, and Li and Luo's forces advanced and occupied the Beidouzhen and Yazi Pond areas, breaking through the 24th Army's first line of defense in Renjing at Laoshukou, Yujia Village, Changshan Bridge, Shuanggufen, and other places, directly threatening the second line of defense. Liu Wenhui was furious and immediately selected 5,000 elite soldiers from his army, organizing a suicide squad divided into plainclothes teams, pistol teams, bomb teams, broadsword teams, and rapid-response teams, launching a five-pronged counterattack against the 21st Army and Li and Luo's forces. They set out late at night on the 26th. The 5,000 desperate men, disregarding everything, charged fiercely at the enemy's positions. Despite constant machine-gun fire, shrapnel, and mortar bombardment, they showed no fear, charging wildly and smashing the 21st Army and Li and Luo's positions to pieces, as if entering an uninhabited area. Liu Xiang, Li Qixiang, Luo Zezhou, and others, seeing the ferocity and unstoppable momentum of the enemy's attack, also selected suicide squads to resist. The fighting continued until the morning of the 27th before both sides ceased operations. In this battle, the 21st Army suffered approximately 4,000 casualties, and Li and Luo's forces suffered approximately 2,000 casualties. Of the 24th Army's 5,000 suicide squad members, only 400 to 500 survived. Liu Wenhui then ordered all units to hold their ground, relying on fortifications to defend their positions and constructing solid fortifications to prepare for a protracted struggle. Seeing this situation, Liu Xiang feared that delaying the matter would create problems. To resolve the situation quickly, he launched a five-pronged attack on the 24th Army. The first route, under the command of Tang Shizun, Chen Lanting, and Mu Zhou, comprised five brigades attacking Jiading with the support of two aircraft. The second route, Pan Wenhua's division of three brigades, attacked Jingyan, also with two aircraft. The third route, Fan Shaozeng's division and the Model Division, comprised six brigades attacking Meishan and Qingshen, with one aircraft. The fourth route, Wang Zunxu's division of four brigades, attacked Renshou, with one aircraft. The fifth route, Li Qixiang and Luo Zezhou's forces, attacked Xinjin and Shuangliu, attacking the 24th Army's rear. With each route properly deployed and heavy troops stationed on the front lines, preparations were made for a major battle. A general mobilization was scheduled for the 29th, with a simultaneous attack on the 24th Army. The battlefront extended over 300 li. The 21st Army's forces deployed to the front lines comprised five divisions and three brigades, totaling approximately 80,000 men, plus Li Qixiang and Luo Zezhou's forces, totaling over 100,000 men. The 24th Army also had approximately 100,000 men, but without aircraft, they found it difficult to resist. Liu Wenhui was quite anxious as a result and convened a military conference in Meishan with his key commanders to discuss countermeasures. The commanders unanimously agreed that the 24th Army was facing extreme danger and that it would be better to endure temporarily and preserve their strength rather than fight bitterly and lose their elite troops. Seeing that his commanders had no intention of fighting again, Liu Wenhui, who was usually headstrong, was also demoralized. He had no choice but to reluctantly comply with his commanders' opinions and negotiate peace with the Chongqing army. He had Leng Yindong and other senior commanders of the 24th Army send a telegram to Liu Xiang, requesting a halt to the attacks. Liu Wenhui also sent Du Shaotang as a representative to meet with Liu Xiang to negotiate everything. As a result, three conditions were agreed upon: (1) The 24th Army would hand over all of its Sichuan defense areas to the Allied Forces and retreat entirely to Xikang; (2) Liu Wenhui would relinquish his positions as commander of the 24th Army and chairman of Sichuan Province. All of his remaining troops would be led by Liu to Xikang; (3) The Allied Forces would recommend to the central government that Liu Wenhui be appointed chairman of Xikang Province and commander-in-chief of the Xikang Border Defense. As for all of Liu's property in Sichuan, the Allied Forces would be responsible for protecting it. After Liu Xiang and Liu Wenhui approved and signed the above three articles, the fighting in the Jiajingren area completely ceased, and both sides stationed themselves on their original lines. Thus, this Sichuan war, which had lasted for nearly three months, finally had hope of ending. Liu Xiang, with this military expedition, aimed to unify the Sichuan situation. Now that a formidable enemy had been eliminated, other armies would be awed and submit. He then initiated a post-war conference in Neijiang to discuss the Sichuan situation, inviting the leaders of the various armies to participate in person. Liu himself had arrived in Neijiang on the 28th. Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, Li Qixiang, and Luo Zezhou also set out. Liu Wenhui sent Leng Yindong and Du Shaotang as representatives. Currently, only Deng Xihou remained in Chengdu, not participating in person but sending Zeng Zhisong as a representative to the meeting. Liu Cunhou's representative, Liu Qian, was in Chengdu and had not yet departed. It is reported that the Chongqing side has largely formulated the issues to be discussed at the meeting, including: (1) resolving the 24th Army case; (2) unifying the Sichuan situation; (3) establishing a sound provincial government; (4) dividing the 24th Army's defense areas; (5) equalizing the Allied Forces' military quotas; (6) determining the Allied Forces' troop stationing; (7) allocating the Allied Forces' military expenses. It is said that Liu Xiang today again telegraphed Deng Xihou and Liu Cunhou, urging them to arrive by a specific date so that they could discuss matters together. There is talk that the meeting is scheduled to open on New Year's Day. Enclosed is Liu Wenhui's telegram of gratitude to Liu Xiang [To Director Liu Fucheng Jun Jian: My uncle and nephew have been at war for two months now. Although Hui has suffered heavy losses, so has nephew. I believe that the Sichuan situation, disorder, people's livelihood withered, and communist party secretly growing, should not continue to war, so Hui has to ask for peace with nephew, immediately cease fighting, discuss the aftermath, our family is engaged in farming for generations, with a pure reputation, from our uncle and two ancestors, gradually ascending to the academy, literary and military separating, and then entering the gentry family with a clean door, harmony, politeness, and harmony, there is a fixed evaluation in the countryside, our generation bears the shadow of our ancestors, should be a thick report of morality, the spirits of ancestors in heaven, how should we work hard with each other, without the shame of family voice, unfortunately my uncle and nephew are facing each other in war, so that all people are suffering, stirring up the red tide, losing shame to the green history, if we silently remember the outside of the fog mountain, where the ancestral tomb is located, the area where we played and fished in childhood, the mountain hermit knows, and should not cry, so Hui does not take seeking peace as shame, and stopping soldiers as cowardice, please nephew stop the soldiers from advancing, and deal with them appropriately, in a hurry, or inevitably straightforward, but also pray for forgiveness, and hope to see teachings, without any task of building and looking forward to it, Wenhui Yin,] (December 29)

Fujian Northern Generals' Bandit Suppression Plan 62

Liu Zhennian's Division Has Been Stationed in Fujian

Fuzhou Correspondence: The northern Fujian Red Bandits were defeated by the joint efforts of Mao Weisou and Liu Heding's two divisions, and Shaowu and Guangze counties were successively recovered. At that time, the northern Fujian Red Bandits retreated into eastern Jiangxi and were intercepted and attacked by Chen Cheng's army. They then fled from Lichuan and Zixi, sneaking into the border between Guangze and Chong'an, looting wantonly. Jianning and Taining counties were still occupied by the rebel soldiers of the former Sun Lianzhong. Although these rebel soldiers claimed to be Red Army soldiers, they were not commanded by Zhu De and had no system. They had already become bandits. A few days ago, generals Mao Weisou, Liu Heding, Zhou Zhiqun, and Qian Yuguang held a military meeting in Shaowu to discuss ways to suppress these scattered bandits. It was decided that in addition to sending troops to guard important cities and towns, each division and brigade would also send out a number of troops to form guerrilla teams, penetrate deep into the bandit areas, track and eliminate them, and strive to clear the bandit traces in the four counties of Guangchong, Jian, and Tai in the shortest possible time. Then, they would contact the Jiangxi army and launch a joint attack on the large bandit gangs. Yesterday, the plan was telegraphed to the Pacification Office for approval. In addition, Liang Lizhu and Zhao Zhenqi's two brigades of Liu Zhennian's 21st Division have successively entered the counties of Pucheng, Songxi, Zhenghe, and Shouning in Fujian from the Zhejiang border. Han Meicen, the representative sent by Liu Zhennian to Fujian, also went from Fuzhou to Yanping to Shaowu to meet Mao Weisou and Liu Heding to discuss defense deployment measures. Also, yesterday, the Provincial Government received a telegram from the Ministry of Military Affairs, informing that Liu's division was transferred to Fujian to suppress the bandits, and the expenses related to departure and supply were to be raised by themselves. If there is any misappropriation from the local area, it should also be returned and padded. As for the Shandong notes brought, Director Liu should negotiate with the local Chamber of Commerce to find a way to cash them on a regular basis to avoid disputes. Past and Present of Jiangxi Province's Russian Black Tea Sales 63

Nanchang Correspondence: Silk, tea, and porcelain are the main export products of our country. Among them, porcelain is unique to Jingdezhen in Jiangxi Province, and tea is also a major product of Jiangxi Province. Russian black tea, produced in Xiushui and Tonggu, ranks first. At this time of Sino-Russian resumption of diplomatic relations and mutual progress in the two countries' commerce, a brief description of the past and present situation of Jiangxi tea is provided below.

Xiushui, Tonggu, Wuning, Fuliang, Dexing, Yushan, and other places in Jiangxi Province are tea-producing areas. The Xiutong area is full of lush tea trees. According to rough estimates, the total tea production of the province in its heyday was about 500,000 boxes (100 catties per box). The average price per box, calculated at 30 yuan, would also be 15 million yuan. In addition to the coarse tea, tea stalks, and green tea sold to various parts of the country and the province, the refined black tea was exclusively sold to Russia, and green tea sold well in Europe, America, Japan, and the Nanyang Islands. Exports abroad were between six million and ten million. According to a survey by the Department of Construction, in 1926, Xiushui and Tonggu counties produced 19,000 boxes of overseas black tea, 7,600 boxes of leaf tea, 51,000 boxes of powdered tea, 12,000 boxes of store tea, 2,100 boxes of tea stalks, and 6,000 boxes of green tea. In that year, the mountain price of overseas black tea was 70 yuan per box. From the mountain to the sales destination, the cost per box was 27 yuan and 78 cents, and the selling price was only 47 yuan and 78 cents. More than 90 tea houses and shops lost 887,593 yuan. In 1927, a total of 52,000 boxes (5 million catties) of the above-mentioned teas were produced. More than 70 tea houses and shops, seeing the excessive losses in the previous year, lowered the mountain price. The mountain price of overseas tea (the essence of tea) was only 30 yuan, plus the cost of more than 27 yuan, the cost was 57 yuan, and the selling price was 75 yuan, with a total profit of 864,279 taels. In 1928, tea shops saw sluggish overseas sales and only produced 22,000 boxes of overseas black tea. The amount of leaf tea, store tea, and green tea sold domestically reached 103,800 boxes. Although the mountain price of overseas tea was only 47 yuan, more than 90 tea shops still lost more than 280,000 taels of regulations. Since then, things have gone from bad to worse. International sales have been completely taken over by Ceylon and Japanese tea. In addition, years of banditry have turned houses into ruins, and the future of the tea industry is unbearable to hear and unbearable in the past and present. According to tea veterans in Xiushui and the provincial capital, (1) farmers have no tea-growing knowledge at all. They only use their spare time from farming to plant on mountain foothills. They do not pay attention to cultivation, pruning, harvesting, or pest control, resulting in low production and poor quality. (2) In terms of roasting, they stick to the old ways. For example, black tea is dried in the sun. If it rains, it will become moldy. How can one expect it to be refined? (3) Tea operators mostly buy and sell empty-handed. Most of their capital comes from loans. If the tea is still in transit, they will mortgage the bill of lading to foreign merchants, suffering all kinds of exploitation. When the goods arrive at the destination, foreign merchants can arbitrarily manipulate and suppress them, and they all lose money. Because of the losses, the transporters add water and tea stalks and change their appearance, using all kinds of tricks to cheat and seek profit, resulting in a loss of trust with foreign merchants. (1) The tea tax used to be very heavy, directly increasing costs and indirectly affecting the livelihoods of tea farmers and tea merchants. In addition, transportation was inconvenient, and extortion along the way was even more unbearable. (4) Our country's tea-growing methods have not been improved, and the authorities are constantly harassing us, so we cannot compete with Ceylon tea. (5) Since 1927, places such as Xiushui, Wuning, and Dexing have mostly been occupied by bandits. The tea is old on the mountain, and no one picks it. Even if there are a few products, merchants and travelers are afraid to travel. The Xiutong tea trees are now only used as fuel. Now that China and Russia have resumed diplomatic relations, if we want to reorganize our forces and revive the tea industry, we should clear all of the above reasons and strive for improvement so that we can develop. It is said that Provincial Chairman Xiong Shihui, in order to develop the tea industry, had a plan to set up a large-scale tea factory in Jiujiang or Xiushui. (1) Establish tea gardens and tea factories, (2) establish a tea industry bank to circulate capital, (3) attract merchants to operate and transport publicly, (4) improve the tea tax, reward exports, and restore the international market. However, it is not known when it will be implemented. (December 27)
